The Origin of the Hyle Theory and the Contradiction of the First Being
Maturidi traces the origin of the hyle theory and its first contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the theory of primordial hyle arises from ignorance and leads to the contradiction of making the transcendent First Being into a mutable substance.

Core Idea
Theory of hyle destroys the First Being's transcendence and leads to self-annihilation.

Imam al-Maturidi begins his refutation by tracing the hyle theory to a misguidance that sought comfort in fantasy. He then exposes how its proponents, under the guise of describing God, ended up describing a primordial matter, thereby stripping the First of its primacy and implying the world's self-annihilation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the flow of Maturidi's argument from the origin of the theory to its first major contradiction.
Notice how Maturidi starts by attributing the theory to ignorance and misguidance.
2
Identify the core contradiction
Focus on the part where Maturidi shows that the hyle theory makes the First Being a substance, then multiple substances, erasing its primacy. This is the first logical flaw.
The First Being is described as beyond accidents and substances, but hyle theory reduces it to a substrate.
3
Reflect on the consequence
Consider Maturidi's point that this leads to the world's annihilation by itself and the transformation of the eternal by accidents.
This shows that the theory is self-defeating.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الفقيه رحمه الله : فمن تأمل ما صار هؤلاء إليه علم أنهم أوتوا ذلك لجهلهم نعم الله فهموا عن سبيل الرشد فضلوا ، ثم بعثتهم حيرة الضلال إلى الاستيناس بمثل هذا الخيال الذى لا يصير عليه عقل ولا يستجلبه هوى ، والله المستعان ولولا ذلك ما الذي كان يعرفهم أن ابتداء العالم ما ذكر ؟ ثم اسمه الذى وصف ليس فيها ثم ذكرا . وعمله الذى نعت ليس في جوهر العالم دليله ولا في السمع احتماله، لكنهم سمعوا قول أهل التوحيد في وصف الله بالذي صفوا به الهيولى عندهم ، ولم ينظروا فيا ألزمهم التقول به ، فرجعوا فنقضوا ما قد أثبتوه ؛ إذ صيروا الذي لذاته خارج عن احتمال الأعراض ممتنع عن معنى الجواهر [ب] ا سير هوا ثم جوهرا ثم جواهر ، ثم صار بحيث لم يبق من أوليته أثر ، وما بقى مما انتهى أمر العالم من القديم والحديث إلا الجواهر والأعراض ، وذهب الذي لم يكن بهذا الوصف، فيكون فى ذلك فناء العالم بنفسه، واستحالة القديم بذاته بأعراض قهرته وأفنته مما لا قيام لها بنفسها . ويكون في ذلك القول بحدث ويكون في ذلك القول بحدث جميع العالم ، الذي دفعهم عظم هذا القول إلى ذلك الخيال ؛ إذ كل ما هو مأخوذ إنما مأخوذ إنما هو عرض وجوهر ، ولم يكن الأول ، ثم يبطل قوله إذا سمى نفسه حكيما ألزم غيره الصدود عن رأيه واتباع هواه بعد قوله : إن الأصل الذى منه كان جاهلا سفيها ، وأن الأعراض هى أغيار ولدتها القوة السقيمة التي لا حكمة فيها ولا علم لديها أحد أبنائها الذي لم ينل شيئا إلا بها ، فمن أين قدم نفسه عليها . وإذا جاز من غير أصل له به ، صار كذلك ، فليقل في جميع العالم بمثل الذي وهو كذلك ، من ، قال بنفسه . ثم لا يخلو القوة التي في قلبت الحيولي من أن يكون ذا سلطان عليها بمائها قلبتها ، فليقل هو فى الله سبحانه أنشأ الهيولى أو ما شاء على وجه ، فيقبل التقليب ويقوم به التركيب ، ثم ليسم بما شاء هو على فناء ما قلبها فإذا بطل الأصل الذى به العالم وهلك ، مع الإحالة أن يهلك القائم بذاته ليكون بهلا كه انقلاب غير وقيامه ، مع ما يكون فى الهيولى تلفها ، فتصير هي بلا قوة التقليب ، فيكون في ذلك إبطال العالم وتقلبه من حال إلى حال دائما ، فدل وجوده على فساد هذا الأصل. مع ما فى الشاهد أن لا يوجد شيء يصير بحيث لم يكن يصلح إلا بحكيم يجعله كذلك ، فثبت أن ابتداء العالم إن صلح أن يحتمل كون هذه الجواهر والأعراض كان كذلك ، كل على جعله يصلح لشي كذلك و بعد ، فإن القوة إذ هى قلبته بالطبع فهى غير مفارقة عنه ، فما بالها خلت عن عملها في القدم ، وذو الطبع لا يخلو عن عمله في الشاهد . على أن الأعراض التي أحدثت إما أن كانت فى الهيولى فيبطل قوله : كانت خالية عنها حتى حدثت ، أو لم يكن فحدثت من غير شيء ؛ إذ وصف القوة بما وصف به الهيولى، ولم يكن فيه أعراض، فثبت أيضا كونها لا عن شيء، وهذا المعنى الزمهم بالقول الذى قالوا ، فبطل بحمد الله
The jurist, may God have mercy on him, said: Whoever contemplates what these people have come to knows that they were given that due to their ignorance of God's blessings; they deviated from the path of right guidance and went astray. Then the confusion of misguidance drove them to find comfort in such a fantasy that no intellect can affirm nor desire attract. And God is the helper. If not for that, what would make them know that the beginning of the world is as they mentioned? Then the name they described is not in it, then memory. And His action that they described has no evidence in the substance of the world, nor is its possibility in revelation. But they heard the saying of the people of tawhid in describing God with what they described the hyle (al-hayula) with, and they did not consider what they were obliged to say by that. So they returned and nullified what they had affirmed; for they made that which by essence is beyond the acceptance of accidents and impossible for the meaning of substances [؟] then substance then substances, then it became such that no trace remained of its primacy, and nothing remained of what the affair of the world ended with from the eternal and the temporal except substances and accidents, and that which was not described by this description vanished. So in that is the annihilation of the world by itself, and the transformation of the eternal in its essence by accidents that overpowered and annihilated it, accidents that have no subsistence by themselves. And in that is the statement of the temporality, and in that is the statement of the temporality of the whole world, which the magnitude of this saying drove them to that fantasy; for everything that is taken is only an accident and substance, and the First was not. Then his saying is invalidated when he calls himself wise, he obliges others to turn away from his opinion and follow his desire after his saying: that the origin from which he came was ignorant and foolish, and that the accidents are changes born of the sick power that has no wisdom nor knowledge, one of its offspring that attained nothing except through it. So from where did he advance himself over them? And if it is permissible from no origin to him, it becomes so, so let him say about the whole world something like that which is so, from, he said by himself. Then the power that is in the core of the hyle is not free from being sovereign over it by its water, it turned it; so let him say about God, may He be exalted, that He originated the hyle or whatever He willed in a manner that accepts turning and composition arises in it, then let him name it as he wills upon the annihilation of what it turned. So when the origin by which the world exists becomes invalid and perishes, along with the impossibility that the self-subsistent perishes so that its destruction is the change of other and its subsistence, along with what occurs in the hyle of its destruction, so it becomes without the power of turning. So in that is the invalidation of the world and its perpetual change from state to state. So its existence indicates the corruption of this origin. Along with what is in the witnessed world: that nothing exists that became such as it was not except it is suitable only by a wise one who makes it so. So it is established that the beginning of the world—if it is plausible that it could be that these substances and accidents were thus, all according to what makes it suitable for something—so and after, for the power, since it turned it by nature, is not separate from it. So why was it empty of its action in pre-eternity? And that which has a nature is not empty of its action in the witnessed world. Moreover, the accidents that were produced: either they were in the hyle, then his saying that it was empty of them until they occurred is invalidated; or they were not, then they occurred from nothing, for he described the power as he described the hyle, and there were no accidents in it. So it is also established that they are from nothing. And this meaning compelled them to the saying they said. So it is invalidated, praise be to God.
Source pages p. 747

Commentary
This passage is a detailed refutation of those who posit a primordial hyle (prime matter) as the substrate of the world. The author, Imam al-Maturidi, begins by stating that those who hold this view have gone astray due to ignorance of God's blessings. They have taken comfort in a fantasy that neither reason nor desire can justify. He then points out that their description of the hyle conflicts with what they claim about God; they borrowed from the people of tawhid but ended up contradicting themselves. The refutation proceeds step by step: First, they made the First Being, which is beyond accidents and substances, into a substance and then multiple substances, destroying its primacy. This leads to the annihilation of the world by itself and the corruption of the eternal by accidents. They also end up implying that the origin is ignorant and foolish, which invalidates their claim that it is wise. Furthermore, the power they posit in the hyle would have to be either separate or inherent, but both options lead to contradictions: if separate, it would have been inactive in pre-eternity; if inherent, then accidents would have always been present, contradicting their claim of origination. The conclusion is that their entire theory is invalid, and the existence of an ordered world proves that it must have been created by a wise creator, not by a blind power.

Key Terms
الهيولى (hyle/al-hayula)
الأعراض (al-a'rad, accidents)
الجواهر (al-jawahir, substances)
الأول (al-awwal, the First)
القديم (al-qadim, the eternal)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the world originates from a primordial matter called hyle which is the substrate of all change.
Correction: This leads to contradictions: the First Being becomes a mutable substance, losing its transcendence, and implies the world's self-annihilation.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the first consequence of positing a primordial hyle?
A) The world becomes eternal.
B) The First Being is made into a substance, losing its primacy.
C) Accidents are proven to be self-subsistent.
D) The wisdom of the creator is affirmed.

Key Takeaway
The theory of hyle contradicts the transcendence of the First Being and implies the world's self-annihilation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Maturidi says these people were given to misguidance due to ignorance of God's blessings. In what area of your life are you ignorant of God's blessings, and how might that ignorance be leading you to accept a false belief about God? Will you actively seek to recognize His blessings today?
?
The proponents borrowed descriptions of God from the people of tawhid but applied them wrongly. Have you ever taken a truth about God and twisted it to fit your own desires or comfort? What will you do to return to the correct understanding?
?
This passage shows that a wrong understanding of God can lead to the annihilation of meaning itself. If you were to describe God in a way that limits His transcendence, what would you be losing in your relationship with Him? Are you willing to repent from that today and submit to His true majesty?

The Problem of Power and the Necessity of a Wise Creator
Maturidi refutes the role of power in hyle and concludes that only a wise creator explains the world.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the arguments against the hyle theory regarding the nature of power and the necessity of a wise creator for the world's order.

Core Idea
Blind power cannot produce an ordered world; only a wise creator can.

Imam al-Maturidi continues his refutation by focusing on the power that supposedly turns the hyle. He shows that this power must be either separate or inherent, both leading to absurdities. He concludes that the existence of an orderly world can only be explained by a wise creator, not a blind power.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on power
Read the Arabic and translation for the second part of the refutation, focusing on the arguments about the power (al-quwwa) that turns the hyle.
Pay attention to the dilemma Maturidi presents.
2
Analyze the dilemma
Maturidi asks: is the power sovereign over hyle or not? If it is, why was it inactive in pre-eternity? If not, then the hyle itself would have accidents eternally.
Both options contradict the theory.
3
Understand the conclusion
Finally, Maturidi argues that the ordered world requires a wise creator, not a blind principle, and that the hyle theory is invalid.
This is the key takeaway.

لديها أحد أبنائها الذي لم ينل شيئا إلا بها ، فمن أين قدم نفسه عليها . وإذا جاز من غير أصل له به ، صار كذلك ، فليقل في جميع العالم بمثل الذي وهو كذلك ، من ، قال بنفسه . ثم لا يخلو القوة التي في قلبت الحيولي من أن يكون ذا سلطان عليها بمائها قلبتها ، فليقل هو فى الله سبحانه أنشأ الهيولى أو ما شاء على وجه ، فيقبل التقليب ويقوم به التركيب ، ثم ليسم بما شاء هو على فناء ما قلبها فإذا بطل الأصل الذى به العالم وهلك ، مع الإحالة أن يهلك القائم بذاته ليكون بهلا كه انقلاب غير وقيامه ، مع ما يكون فى الهيولى تلفها ، فتصير هي بلا قوة التقليب ، فيكون في ذلك إبطال العالم وتقلبه من حال إلى حال دائما ، فدل وجوده على فساد هذا الأصل. مع ما فى الشاهد أن لا يوجد شيء يصير بحيث لم يكن يصلح إلا بحكيم يجعله كذلك ، فثبت أن ابتداء العالم إن صلح أن يحتمل كون هذه الجواهر والأعراض كان كذلك ، كل على جعله يصلح لشي The jurist, may God have mercy on him, said: Whoever contemplates what these people have come to knows that they were given that due to their ignorance of God's blessings; they deviated from the path of right guidance and went astray. Then the confusion of misguidance drove them to find comfort in such a fantasy that no intellect can affirm nor desire attract. And God is the helper. If not for that, what would make them know that the beginning of the world is as they mentioned? Then the name they described is not in it, then memory. And His action that they described has no evidence in the substance of the world, nor is its possibility in revelation. But they heard the saying of the people of tawhid in describing God with what they described the hyle (al-hayula) with, and they did not consider what they were obliged to say by that. So they returned and nullified what they had affirmed; for they made that which by essence is beyond the acceptance of accidents and impossible for the meaning of substances [؟] then substance then substances, then it became such that no trace remained of its primacy, and nothing remained of what the affair of the world ended with from the eternal and the temporal except substances and accidents, and that which was not described by this description vanished. So in that is the annihilation of the world by itself, and the transformation of the eternal in its essence by accidents that overpowered and annihilated it, accidents that have no subsistence by themselves. And in that is the statement of the temporality, and in that is the statement of the temporality of the whole world, which the magnitude of this saying drove them to that fantasy; for everything that is taken is only an accident and substance, and the First was not. Then his saying is invalidated when he calls himself wise, he obliges others to turn away from his opinion and follow his desire after his saying: that the origin from which he came was ignorant and foolish, and that the accidents are changes born of the sick power that has no wisdom nor knowledge, one of its offspring that attained nothing except through it. So from where did he advance himself over them? And if it is permissible from no origin to him, it becomes so, so let him say about the whole world something like that which is so, from, he said by himself. Then the power that is in the core of the hyle is not free from being sovereign over it by its water, it turned it; so let him say about God, may He be exalted, that He originated the hyle or whatever He willed in a manner that accepts turning and composition arises in it, then let him name it as he wills upon the annihilation of what it turned. So when the origin by which the world exists becomes invalid and perishes, along with the impossibility that the self-subsistent perishes so that its destruction is the change of other and its subsistence, along with what occurs in the hyle of its destruction, so it becomes without the power of turning. So in that is the invalidation of the world and its perpetual change from state to state. So its existence indicates the corruption of this origin. So why was it empty of its action in pre-eternity? And that which has a nature is not empty of its action in the witnessed world. Moreover, the accidents that were produced: either they were in the hyle, then his saying that it was empty of them until they occurred is invalidated; or they were not, then they occurred from nothing, for he described the power as he described the hyle, and there were no accidents in it. So it is also established that they are from nothing. And this meaning compelled them to the saying they said. So it is invalidated, praise be to God.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed refutation of those who posit a primordial hyle (prime matter) as the substrate of the world. They have taken comfort in a fantasy that neither reason nor desire can justify. He then points out that their description of the hyle conflicts with what they claim about God; they borrowed from the people of tawhid but ended up contradicting themselves. The refutation proceeds step by step: First, they made the First Being, which is beyond accidents and substances, into a substance and then multiple substances, destroying its primacy. Second Argument Against the Hyle Theory
Maturidi refutes hyle theory via the concept of power and cites Ibn Shabib's view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of the hyle theory by showing the incoherence of the concept of 'power' and the inconsistency among its proponents.

Core Idea
If power is separate from hyle, duality arises; if identical, it is self-contradiction.

Imam Maturidi presents a logical dismantling of the hyle theory by examining the 'power' they posit as the agent of change. He shows that this power cannot coherently be distinct from nor identical to the hyle. Then he notes the discord among hyle theorists, as Muhammad ibn Shabib redefines power as movement, revealing confusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of the argument, then read the literal translation. Notice the dense logical style.
The Arabic contains several conditional statements; take your time.
2
Identify the two possibilities for power
The argument presents a dilemma: the power is either other than the hyle or identical to it. Locate these two branches in the text.
Look for phrases like 'غير الهيولى' and 'هي هيولى'.
3
Follow the logical consequences
If power is distinct, then there are two things (hyle and power), introducing number and event. If identical, then the hyle turns itself, which is absurd. Work through these implications.
The absurdity is that the power cannot turn itself without being both agent and patient.
4
Consider the critique of accidents
Maturidi argues that the accidents said to arise from power cannot coherently move or still the hyle without an external cause or direction.
This reinforces the incoherence of the hyle theory.
5
Examine Muhammad ibn Shabib's view
Note that Ibn Shabib calls the power 'movement' but in his narration it is indescribable. This shows disagreement among the proponents.
This inconsistency undermines the theory's credibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على أنه أمكن القلب عليهم فى كل ما قالوا للقوة أن يجعل ذلك للهيولى في القوة ، على أنها لا تخلو من غير أن يكون غير الهيولى ، فها اثنان ، وزعم الكم من باب العدد ، فلم يكن فلم يكن ثمة حدث ، وقد أوجب هنالك ، أو هي هيولى . فيبطل قوله : هي مع الهيولى ، أو هى التي قلبت الهيولى ، وكأنها قلبت نفسها لا الهيولى . مع ما زعم أن تلك الأعراض اعترضت في الهيولى فحركته وسكنته ودفعته وخفضته من غير أن كان ثمة غير إليه تتحرك أو فيه يسكن أو إليه يرتفع وينحط ، و وجود أمثال فاسد فما عنه تولده ، فهي في أصله أشد فسادا وزعم محمد بن شبيب أنه أنه يسمى القوة حركة ، وفى روايته أنها لا توصف
Moreover, it is possible to refute them in everything they said: that they attribute that to the power for the hyle in the power, on the basis that [the power] is not free from being other than the hyle, so here are two. And he claimed quantity from the category of number, so there was not, so there was no event, and he necessitated there, or it is hyle. So his saying is invalidated: 'it is with the hyle,' or 'it is that which turned the hyle,' as if it turned itself, not the hyle. Along with what he claimed: that those accidents occurred in the hyle and moved it, stilled it, pushed it, and lowered it without there being any other to which it moves or in which it rests or toward which it rises and falls. And the existence of such things is corrupt, so what is generated from it is more corrupt in its origin. And Muhammad ibn Shabib claimed that he calls the power 'movement,' and in his narration that it is not described.
Source pages p. 748

Commentary
This passage contains a second, more specific argument against the hyle theory and then cites the opinion of Muhammad ibn Shabib. The argument proceeds by considering the 'power' (قوة) that the hyle theorists posit as the agent of change. If this power is other than the hyle, then there are two distinct things (hyle and power). If they are two, then there is a kind of duality that introduces number, and the power would be either eternal or temporal—both problematic. If the power is not other, then it is the hyle itself, so the hyle turns itself, which is absurd. Furthermore, the accidents that arise from this power are said to move or still the hyle without any external mover or goal, which is incoherent. The author then notes that Muhammad ibn Shabib called this power 'movement' (حركة), but in his narration it is not described (i.e., it is unknowable). This shows the confusion among the proponents of the theory.

Key Terms
القوة
العدد
الحدث
الحركة
محمد بن شبيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The 'power' in hyle theory is a coherent explanatory concept for change in matter.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the concept of power leads to contradictions: if distinct from hyle it introduces duality and events, if identical it leads to absurd self-action. Moreover, its proponents disagree on its definition, undermining its coherence.

Checkpoint
What does Muhammad ibn Shabib call the 'power' in the hyle theory, according to this passage?
A) Substance
B) Accident
C) Movement
D) Hyle

Key Takeaway
The hyle theory collapses because its concept of 'power' is either redundant or self-contradictory, and even its proponents disagree on its definition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hold a belief that seems to explain something, do you ever stop to check whether it actually creates more contradictions than it solves? What belief in your life might need such a test today?
?
The hyle theorists introduced 'power' to fix a problem, but their own account collapsed. Are there areas in your faith or practice where you rely on vague concepts without truly understanding them? Will you take time to clarify them?
?
Even the proponents disagreed—Ibn Shabib called it 'movement' but left it undescribed. How often do you accept an argument because it's common or old, without verifying its internal consistency? What will you do differently this week?

Refuting the Samaniyya: Al-Nazzam's Debate
Al-Nazzam refutes Samaniyya's claim of earth's natural fall.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Samaniyya's argument for the earth's natural fall and al-Nazzam's initial refutation.

Core Idea
Heaviness alone does not explain why the earth does not fall.

The Samaniyya, a materialist sect, argued that the earth continuously falls because of its natural heaviness. This lesson presents al-Nazzam's critical response, which exposes the weaknesses in their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: claim, response, counter-response.
The debate is quick and seems playful to the author.
2
Identify the Samaniyya claim
Find where the Samaniyya state that the earth falls by its nature. What reason do they give?
They argue based on heaviness.
3
Understand al-Nazzam's counter-arguments
Al-Nazzam presents two examples: a stone with a feather, and the wind lifting objects. How do these challenge the claim?
He shows that weight alone doesn't determine falling.
4
Reflect on the author's verdict
The author dismisses the debate as 'like playing'. Why? What is missing from their reasoning?
The debate lacks a proper foundation in observation of the whole cosmos.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة أقاويل السمنية من الدهرية وبيان فسادها. وقالت السمنية من الدهرية، مع موافقتهم في حدوث الأشياء في الأزل، إن الأرض لا تزال تهوى سفلا بمن عليها. فسألهم عن ذلك النظام، فاحتجوا بثقلها، والثقيل لا يقاوم الهواء ولا يقوم في الجو. فعارضهم بسرعة انحدار الحجر بثقله إذا أرسل مع الريشة، ثم كانت الأرض منها أثقل، وقد أدركاها. ثم عارضهم بما رأوا الريح تحمل الشيء فتصعد به في العلو دون الجوانب، فما يدريكم لو كانت تحت الأرض فتحملها بقوتها، فكيف حكمتم بان يهوى دون أن يصعد ويرتفع، وقد رأيتم مثله، وقطع الكلام على هذا. وإذا كان ذا حاصل المناظرة فما أشبهها بالملاعبة، بل الأصل إذ كنا نعاين السماء منذ عاينها على حالة واحدة، وعاينا الأرض على ثقلها، وعلى ما كان كل جزء من أجوائها لو أرسل من أعلى موضع يبلغه الوهم لكان يلحقها دل أن الأرض إذ قرت على حال وكذلك السماء، وهما في طبيعتها بطبع الثقل وأن لا قرار لهما في الهواء، ثبت أن قرارهما بقوى حكيم، وأنه منشئها على ما لا وهم يدركه الأوهام ولا يبلغه العقول، وفى ذلك بطلان الدهر وفروعه. ما كانت مناظرة هؤلاء عبثا، أو طريقها البحث عن الأمور الخفية لتنجلي، وعن الوقوف على حدود الحكمة جعلوا العالم على ما عليه من بنى السمنية هو بوداسف، وعلى هذا المذهب أكثر أهل بلاد ما وراء النهر قبل الإسلام، ومعنى السمنية منسوب إلى سمى، وهم أسخى أهل الأرض والأديان، ومذهبهم يقوم على دفع الشيطان.
Section: The sayings of the Samaniyya from the Dahriyya and the demonstration of their corruption. The Samaniyya from the Dahriyya said, while agreeing with [others] on the temporal origination of things in pre-eternity, that the earth continues to fall downward with whatever is upon it. So al-Nazzam asked them about that, and they argued by its heaviness, and the heavy cannot resist the air nor stay in the air. He countered them with the speed of descent of a stone by its weight when released with a feather, then the earth is heavier than them, and it has overtaken them. Then he countered them with what they saw of the wind carrying something and raising it up high without the sides, so how do you know if it were under the earth it would carry it by its force? So how did you rule that it falls without ascending and rising, while you have seen the like of it? And the speech was cut short on this. And if this is the outcome of the debate, then it is like playing. Rather, the principle is: since we observe the sky from when we observed it in one state, and we observe the earth in its heaviness, and that every part of its atmosphere if released from the highest point that imagination reaches would catch up to it, indicates that the earth settled in a state, and likewise the sky, while both are in their nature of heaviness and that they have no stability in the air, then their stability is established by the power of a wise [agent], and that He is their originator in what neither imaginations perceive nor intellects reach. And in that is the invalidity of the Dahriyya and its branches. The debate of these people was not in vain, rather its way is the investigation of hidden matters to become clear, and of standing upon the limits of wisdom. They made the world as it is from the Samaniyya: he is Budasaf, and upon this madhhab were most people of Transoxiana before Islam, and the meaning of Samaniyya is attributed to Sam, and they are the most generous of the people of the earth and religions, and their madhhab is based on repelling the shaitan.
Source pages p. 751

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Samaniyya, a sect of the Dahriyya (materialists) who believed the earth naturally falls downward. Al-Nazzam is cited as engaging them in debate. The Samaniyya argued from the heaviness of the earth, claiming that a heavy object cannot resist the air and thus must fall. Al-Nazzam countered with examples: a stone and a feather—the stone falls faster despite both being subject to air resistance; and the wind can lift objects upward, showing that air can support weight. He questioned why they assume the wind could not also lift the earth. The author then presents the correct proof: careful observation shows that both the earth and sky remain stable despite their heaviness and the fact that they have no natural place in the air. This stability can only be due to the power of a wise creator who sustains them in ways beyond human imagination and intellect. This refutes all materialist branches. The passage concludes with historical notes about the Samaniyya: their founder Budasaf, their prevalence in Transoxiana before Islam, and their doctrine of repelling the shaitan.

Key Terms
السمنية
الدهرية
النظام
الثقل
الهواء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the earth falls by its natural heaviness without external cause.
Correction: Heaviness alone does not explain the earth's motion; observation shows air can support weight, and the earth is stable.

Checkpoint
How does al-Nazzam refute the Samaniyya argument that the earth falls by its heaviness?
A) By comparing the descent of a stone and a feather, showing that if the earth were naturally falling it would not be stable.
B) By asserting that the earth is light.
C) By denying heaviness altogether.
D) By appealing to scripture.

Key Takeaway
The Samaniyya's argument from heaviness is insufficient; al-Nazzam's examples show the need for a deeper explanation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that a simple, obvious explanation (like 'heaviness causes falling') is the full truth, without considering hidden factors? In what area of your life might you be making this same mistake right now?
?
The Samaniyya saw the earth's fall as inevitable based on their observation, yet they ignored the counterexamples. Is there a belief you hold that you've never tested against opposing evidence? Will you actively seek out that evidence today?
?
Al-Nazzam didn't offer a new theory—he only exposed the flaw in their reasoning. How often do you defend your opinions without examining their foundation? What is one belief you can honestly challenge this week?

The True Proof: Stability as Divine Sign
Maturidi's proof of a creator from the stability of earth and sky.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that the observed stability of the earth and sky points to a wise creator.

Core Idea
What looks natural is actually sustained by a wise Creator.

After dismissing the debate as futile, Maturidi presents the real argument: the fact that the heavy earth and sky remain in place, against their natural tendency, proves they are upheld by an external power — the Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof passage
Read the Arabic from 'بل الأصل' to the end. Notice how Maturidi moves from observation to conclusion.
This is a concise philosophical argument.
2
Identify the observations
What do we observe about the sky and earth? They have been in the same state, and the earth is heavy.
3
Follow the inference
Since heavy objects have no natural stability in the air, their actual stability shows they are held in place by a powerful, wise agent.
This agent must be beyond normal perception.
4
Connect to refuting the Dahriyya
Maturidi concludes that this invalidates all materialistic worldviews. How?
Because materialists deny any external cause for natural order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة أقاويل السمنية من الدهرية وبيان فسادها. وقالت السمنية من الدهرية، مع موافقتهم في حدوث الأشياء في الأزل، إن الأرض لا تزال تهوى سفلا بمن عليها. فسألهم عن ذلك النظام، فاحتجوا بثقلها، والثقيل لا يقاوم الهواء ولا يقوم في الجو. فعارضهم بسرعة انحدار الحجر بثقله إذا أرسل مع الريشة، ثم كانت الأرض منها أثقل، وقد أدركاها. ثم عارضهم بما رأوا الريح تحمل الشيء فتصعد به في العلو دون الجوانب، فما يدريكم لو كانت تحت الأرض فتحملها بقوتها، فكيف حكمتم بان يهوى دون أن يصعد ويرتفع، وقد رأيتم مثله، وقطع الكلام على هذا. وإذا كان ذا حاصل المناظرة فما أشبهها بالملاعبة، بل الأصل إذ كنا نعاين السماء منذ عاينها على حالة واحدة، وعاينا الأرض على ثقلها، وعلى ما كان كل جزء من أجوائها لو أرسل من أعلى موضع يبلغه الوهم لكان يلحقها دل أن الأرض إذ قرت على حال وكذلك السماء، وهما في طبيعتها بطبع الثقل وأن لا قرار لهما في الهواء، ثبت أن قرارهما بقوى حكيم، وأنه منشئها على ما لا وهم يدركه الأوهام ولا يبلغه العقول، وفى ذلك بطلان الدهر وفروعه. ما كانت مناظرة هؤلاء عبثا، أو طريقها البحث عن الأمور الخفية لتنجلي، وعن الوقوف على حدود الحكمة جعلوا العالم على ما عليه من بنى السمنية هو بوداسف، وعلى هذا المذهب أكثر أهل بلاد ما وراء النهر قبل الإسلام، ومعنى السمنية منسوب إلى سمى، وهم أسخى أهل الأرض والأديان، ومذهبهم يقوم على دفع الشيطان.

?

?
The argument refutes materialism by showing that the world cannot be self-sufficient. Is there any part of your life where you live as if you are self-sufficient, forgetting that every moment is sustained by the Creator? What is one concrete step you will take today to live in that awareness?

The Sophist Denial of Knowledge and Ibn Shabib's Rebuttal
Maturidi reports the Sophist claim and Ibn Shabib's self-refutation argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sophist argument against the possibility of knowledge and how Ibn Shabib refuted it by exposing its self-contradictory nature.

Core Idea
The claim 'There is no knowledge' self-destructs: asserting it requires knowledge.

The Sophists argued that all cognition is mere belief because our senses and experiences are contradictory. Ibn Shabib, however, pointed out a fatal flaw: the very statement 'there is no knowledge' must be known to be asserted, thus affirming knowledge. This lesson traces that logical move.

Guided Path
1
Read the Sophist claim
The Sophists list examples of contradiction (e.g., a bat seeing at night but not day) to conclude that knowledge is impossible and only belief exists. Read their argument carefully.
Note that their claim is based on empirical variability, not on a logical premise.
2
Identify Ibn Shabib's question
Ibn Shabib poses a dilemma: either the Sophists know their own statement (thus affirming knowledge) or they do not know it (making their claim baseless). Identify both horns.
This is a classic 'self-refutation' argument (elenchus).
3
Understand the logical force
If they say they know, they have proven knowledge exists. If they say they don't know, they have no ground to call others to their view. Therefore, their position is untenable.
The phrase 'ألزموا السكت' means they are forced into silence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ رحمه الله : قالت السوفسطائية : لما وجدنا الإنسان يعلم شيئا ثم يبطل ، ويجد لذة ثم يزول، ويهلك هوام البر في البحر ، والبحر في البر ، ويبصر الخفاش بالليل ويغشى بالنهار ثبت أن لا يصح علم ، وإنما هو اعتقاد لا غير وإن اختلف عن اعتقاد غيره فسأل ابن شبيب فقال : قولكم لا علم ، يعلم قلتم فقد أثبتم ، أو لا يعلم ، لم يكن لكم الدعاء إليه ، مع ما علمتم أنكم قلتم بغير علم ، فإن قالوا بالعلم أثبتوا العلم ، وإن قالوا بالثاني ألزموا السكت ، وذا مجرى الباب . قال الشيخ رحمه الله : ومناظرة من يقول بهذا الكلام لا معنى ل[؟] لأنه يحصل على أنه اعتقاد لا علم ، فكل شيء يقول عند المناظرة فهو ذلك ، وإنما يناظر مثل من ينفي الحقائق حتى يرد قوله محققا وكذلك بدعواه ، وأما من يقول : ليس غير الاعتقاد ، فهو أي شيء يقول فانما هو ذلك ، وإنما يقابل بالضرب المؤلم والقطع ، ويعتقد ما يعتقده هو ، فينكر عليه بضده أو بقوله إني أعتقد انكارك إقرارا ، حتى يدفعه الضرورة إلى الاقرار بما أنكر من طلب النحس . ما أنه اعتقاد لا غير ، وفي ذلك اثبات الاعتقاد ، فيبطل قوله بنفي العلم باثبات الاعتقاد ، والله الموفق
The Shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: The Sophists said: Since we find that a person knows something then it becomes invalid, and experiences pleasure then it disappears, and the predators of land perish in the sea and those of sea on land, and the bat sees at night and is dazzled by day, it is established that knowledge is not valid; rather it is only belief, no more, even if it differs from the belief of another. So Ibn Shabib asked and said: Your statement 'there is no knowledge' — if you know [that you said it], then you have affirmed knowledge; or if you do not know, then you have no basis to call [others] to it, given that you know that you spoke without knowledge. If they say it with knowledge, they have affirmed knowledge; and if they say it with the second [i.e., without knowledge], they are obliged to be silent, and that is the course of the matter. The Shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: Arguing with one who says this speech is meaningless because it results in it being belief not knowledge, so everything he says in debate is that [i.e., belief]. One only debates with someone who denies realities so that his statement is returned verified, and likewise his claim. As for one who says there is nothing but belief, whatever he says is only that, and he should be met with painful beating and cutting, and he believes what he believes, so one denies it with its opposite or with his statement 'I believe your denial is affirmation', until necessity drives him to affirm what he denied in seeking disaster. That it is belief only, and in that is affirmation of belief, so his statement is invalidated by negating knowledge through affirming belief. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 752

Commentary
This passage presents the claim of the Sophists (al-Sūfisṭā’iyya) that knowledge is impossible, based on empirical contradictions (things changing, animals dying in wrong environments, bats seeing at night but not day). They conclude that all cognition is mere belief (iʿtiqād), not veridical knowledge. Maturidi then reports Ibn Shabib's refutation: The Sophist's own statement 'there is no knowledge' is self-defeating. If they know they said it, they have affirmed knowledge. If they do not know, their claim is baseless. The argument is a classic self-refutation (elenchus). Maturidi adds that debating such a person is pointless because any statement they make is just their belief, so one cannot establish truth. Instead, the appropriate response is physical coercion to force them to admit what they deny. Nonetheless, even their denial of knowledge inadvertently affirms belief, and since belief is a kind of cognition, the negation of knowledge is refuted by the affirmation of belief, which itself requires some knowledge. The passage thus guards against radical skepticism by showing its performative contradiction.

Key Terms
السوفسطائية (al-Sūfisṭā’iyya)
علم (ʿilm)
اعتقاد (iʿtiqād)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Sophist argument seems plausible because of apparent contradictions in experience.
Correction: Ibn Shabib shows that the claim itself requires knowledge, so the argument cannot stand.

Checkpoint
What is the core logical problem with the Sophist claim 'there is no knowledge'?
A) It contradicts religious texts.
B) It is a claim that must be known to be stated, thus affirming knowledge.
C) It is based on faulty observation.
D) It leads to solipsism.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Shabib's refutation shows that the denial of knowledge is self-defeating because the very act of denial presupposes knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Is there any area of your life where you act as if 'knowledge is impossible'—for example, by avoiding deep study because you think certainty is unattainable? What would Ibn Shabib say to you about that avoidance?
?
When you share your Islamic beliefs with others, do you sometimes feel unsure whether you truly know them, or are you relying on assumptions? How does this lesson challenge you to seek certain knowledge before calling others?
?
If you were to apply Ibn Shabib's question to your own most firmly held conviction—'Do I know this, or just believe it?'—how would you answer? And what would that answer demand of you today?

Maturidi on the Futility of Debating Skeptics
Maturidi discusses the futility of debating radical skeptics and advocates physical response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi considered rational debate with radical skeptics useless and how physical coercion can serve as a last resort to force acknowledgment of knowledge.

Core Idea
When skeptics deny all knowledge, only physical compulsion can break their stubbornness.

After presenting Ibn Shabib's logical refutation, Maturidi considers the case of those who insist that all is mere belief. He explains that debating them is futile because every statement they make is just belief. Instead, they should be subjected to painful punishment to force them to admit what they deny, inadvertently affirming the existence of knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read Maturidi's commentary
Maturidi distinguishes between two types of deniers: those who deny realities but can be logically refuted, and those who say only belief exists. Focus on the latter.
The first type can be debated because they accept some truth; the second cannot.
2
Identify the recommended response
For the one who says 'nothing but belief', Maturidi says he should be met with painful beating and cutting. Why? Because his claim makes rational discourse impossible.
The goal is to force him to contradict himself.
3
Understand the final argument
Even in asserting 'only belief', he affirms belief, which is a kind of cognition. This undermines his denial of knowledge because belief itself implies some awareness.
This is a secondary logical refutation complementing the physical force.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: The Sophists said: Since we find that a person knows something then it becomes invalid, and experiences pleasure then it disappears, and the predators of land perish in the sea and those of sea on land, and the bat sees at night and is dazzled by day, it is established that knowledge is not valid; rather it is only belief, no more, even if it differs from the belief of another. So Ibn Shabib asked and said: Your statement 'there is no knowledge' — if you know [that you said it], then you have affirmed knowledge; or if you do not know, then you have no basis to call [others] to it, given that you know that you spoke without knowledge. The Shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: Arguing with one who says this speech is meaningless because it results in it being belief not knowledge, so everything he says in debate is that [i.e., belief]. One only debates with someone who denies realities so that his statement is returned verified, and likewise his claim. As for one who says there is nothing but belief, whatever he says is only that, and he should be met with painful beating and cutting, and he believes what he believes, so one denies it with its opposite or with his statement 'I believe your denial is affirmation', until necessity drives him to affirm what he denied in seeking disaster. That it is belief only, and in that is affirmation of belief, so his statement is invalidated by negating knowledge through affirming belief. And God is the Grantor of success.

Commentary
This passage presents the claim of the Sophists (al-Sūfisṭā’iyya) that knowledge is impossible, based on empirical contradictions (things changing, animals dying in wrong environments, bats seeing at night but not day). They conclude that all cognition is mere belief (iʿtiqād), not veridical knowledge. مناظرة (munāẓara)
اعتقاد (iʿtiqād)
حقيقة (ḥaqīqa)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The only refutation of skepticism is physical force.
Correction: Maturidi also provides a logical refutation: affirming belief implies knowledge.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi consider rational debate with someone who says 'there is nothing but belief' to be meaningless?
A) Because such a person is too stubborn to listen.
B) Because every statement that person makes is itself mere belief, so there is no common ground for truth.
C) Because the person is mentally ill.
D) Because debating would give legitimacy to falsehood.

Key Takeaway
When skeptics deny all knowledge, rational debate fails; physical compulsion can force an admission that inadvertently affirms knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been so convinced of your own opinion that you refused to admit any objective truth, even when faced with evidence? How does Maturidi's description of the skeptic mirror that attitude, and what pain would it take to break your stubbornness?
?
Think of a person in your life who denies obvious truths to avoid changing their behavior. Are you willing to engage them rationally, or do you secretly wish you could force them to see reality? What does this lesson say about both approaches?
?
Is there an area of your faith where you treat your beliefs as mere opinions rather than certain knowledge? How would you feel if someone used physical coercion to make you admit that you do know it? Would that reveal something about the strength of your conviction?

beginner
5 min
Maturidi's Refutation of Naturalistic Explanations
Maturidi refutes Sumaniyya naturalism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi dismisses naturalistic causal explanations for animal characteristics and affirms that such realities are simply matters of divine creation.

Core Idea
Naturalistic explanations are futile; the true cause is Allah's creation.

In this passage, Maturidi reports the arguments of the Sumaniyya, a materialist sect that attributed biological differences to the dominance of natural elements. He then dismisses their entire approach as frivolous, asserting that the correct position is simply that things are as they are by divine decree.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Maturidi first presents the Sumaniyya's views before dismissing them.
2
Identify the Sumaniyya's claims
The Sumaniyya explain fish, otter, bat, and lion based on dominance of natural opposites (cold/moist, heat/dry) and light sensitivity. List each example and its explanation.
3
Locate Maturidi's rebuttal
Find the phrase 'وذلك كله عبث' and understand its meaning: 'all that is frivolous.' Note that he does not engage in a detailed refutation but dismisses the entire approach.
This shows Maturidi's methodological stance: naturalist speculation is futile.
4
Reflect on the deeper meaning
Consider why Maturidi calls these explanations futile. How does this relate to the Islamic belief in divine creation and causality?
The lesson is that the real cause is Allah's will, not inherent natures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم تكلف نوع ما كلم النظام السمنية مما لا يجدي نفعا، فزعم أن الحيتان كان الغلبة فى طبائعها الرطوبة والبرودة، فإذا صارت إلى الجدب، والغالب عليه الحرارة واليبوسة غلبتا على الرطوبة والندوة فأهلكا . وكذلك كل متضادين من الطبائع إذا غلب واحد ضده أهلكه . وكذلك أمر الطائر في السماء وكلب الماء فإنه أشد اعتدالا من الحوت، يعيش في الماء والبر، والجتماش فإن بصره مسترقة ليست بالقوية، يذهبه ضوء الشمس، نحو ما يعشى الرجل إذا نظر إلى عين، فإذا غابت الشمس ذهب ما أضعف بصره فأبصر، فإذا اشتدت الظلمة لا يبصر. وأما الأسد فهو قوى البصر، يبصر بالنهار، وأكثر ما يبصر غيره، وكذلك المانع له بالليل أقل مما يمنع غيره . قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : وذلك كله عبث، بل القول إنه كذلك
Then he undertook a kind of argument against the Sumaniyya that does not benefit. He claimed that in fish, the dominance in their natures is moisture and cold; so when they go to dry land, and what dominates there is heat and dryness, they overcome the moisture and dew and destroy them. Likewise, every pair of opposites among natures, if one overcomes its opposite, it destroys it. And likewise the case of the bird in the sky and the water dog (otter), for it is more balanced than the fish; it lives in water and on land. And the bat, its sight is weak, not strong; the light of the sun overpowers it, like a man who is dazzled when he looks at the sun's eye; so when the sun sets, that which weakened his sight goes away and he sees; but when darkness intensifies, he does not see. As for the lion, its sight is strong; it sees by day, and sees more than others; likewise, the hindrance to it at night is less than what hinders others. Abu Mansur, may Allah have mercy on him, said: All that is frivolous; rather, the statement is that it is so.
Source pages p. 754

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Sumaniyya (a materialist or naturalist group) who attempted to explain biological differences by natural causes like dominance of elements. Maturidi reports their claim: fish have moist and cold natures, so on dry land they are overcome by heat and dryness and die; similarly for all opposites. They extend this to the bird, the otter (كلب الماء), the bat, and the lion, each with explanations based on elemental balance, light sensitivity, etc. Maturidi dismisses all this as 'عبث' (frivolous or futile) and simply asserts that the correct statement is that 'it is so' (إنه كذلك), implying these are created realities known by observation, and the speculative naturalistic explanations are unnecessary. The passage shows the author's method: he presents the opponent's view, then rejects it summarily rather than engaging in detailed refutation.

Key Terms
سمنية
طبائع
غلبة
عبث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That naturalistic explanations based on elemental dominance adequately explain animal characteristics.
Correction: Maturidi dismisses such explanations as futile because they ignore divine creation; the correct understanding is that things are as they are by Allah's will.

Checkpoint
How does Maturidi describe the Sumaniyya's arguments?
A) Beneficial
B) Frivolous
C) Persuasive
D) Logical

Key Takeaway
Maturidi rejects naturalistic explanations as futile and affirms that the true cause of all phenomena is Allah's will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time when you explained something as 'just a natural coincidence' or 'luck' without remembering Allah’s will. How does Maturidi's verdict of 'عبث' challenge you to see that event differently? This week, what specific situation will you consciously say 'بل القول إنه كذلك' and attribute directly to Allah?
?
Maturidi called the Sumaniyya's detailed reasoning 'frivolous'. Are there areas of your life where you trust your own logic more than Allah's decree? Write down one belief or habit you have that relies on naturalistic justifications, and commit to replacing it with tawakkul (reliance on Allah).
?
If you truly internalized that 'the true cause is Allah's creation', how would your response to hardships change? Describe one difficulty you are facing now and what it would mean to say 'the statement is that it is so' while turning to Allah instead of seeking only physical remedies.

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
6 min
The Manichaean Doctrine of Light and Darkness
Maturidi expounds the Manichaean cosmology of light and darkness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key tenets of Manichaean dualism as presented by Maturidi, including the nature of light and darkness, their mixture, and the five kinds and senses.

Core Idea
Dualism collapses under its own contradictions.

Maturidi begins by laying out the Manichaean worldview in his own words. He describes a universe composed of two eternal principles: light (good) and darkness (evil). Their mixture produces the world we inhabit. This exposition sets the stage for a logical refutation that requires no external proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the exposition carefully
Read the passage from the beginning to the description of the return of each element to its place. Note the main claims about light and darkness.
This is a detailed cosmological account.
2
Identify the five kinds and five senses
The passage mentions five colors and five senses for each principle. Try to list them and understand their significance in the Manichaean system.
These are used to classify all phenomena.
3
Understand the role of the serpent spirit
Note that darkness has a spirit called 'Hammāma', a serpent that seeks to imprison light. This sets up the purpose of the world.
The serpent is a key agent in the mixture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في صفة أقاويل الثنوية أولاً، أقاويل المنانية وبيان فسادها. قال الشيخ رحمه الله: زعمت المنانية أن الأشياء على ما عليه من امتزاج النور والظلمة، وكانا متباينين: النور في العلو لا يتناهى في أربع جهات شمال وجنوب وصبا ودبور، والظلمة في السفل كذلك، ولها من جهة الالتقاء تناه، فقبعت الظلمة على النور فامتزجا، فكان العالم من امتزاجها على قدر الامتزاج، ولكل واحد منها خمسة أجناس: حمرة وبياض وصفرة وسواد وخضرة، فكل شيء مما جاء من هذا الجنس من جوهر النور فهو خير، وما كان من جوهر الظلمة فهو شر. وكذلك لكل واحد منها حواس خمس: سمع وبصر وذائق وحاسة الشم واللمس، فما أدرك جوهر النور بها فهو خير، وما أدرك جوهر الظلمة فهو شر. وللنور روح، وللظلمة روح، وروح الظلمة يسمى همامة، وهي حية، فغلب العالم ليحبس النور فيها، والنور ليس بحساس، وما كان منه يكون بالطبع ويكون خيرا كله، والهامة حساسة، وسيصير كل واحد منها إلى حيزه. ثم وجد الأشياء أصفاها، وأسفلها أكدرها، ومن طبعها الخفة والثقل، وأمرهما على التنافر، إذ الخفيف يعلو صعدا والثقيل ينحدر سفلا، فيمر الدهر، إذ كانا كذلك يتخلصان من وجه التناهى كما امتزجا. قال الشيخ رحمه الله: ومن تأمل القول وجده كله متناقضا، من غير أن يحتاج إلى تكلف الدلالة على إبطال القول سوى تفسيره. أول شيء به أنه أراك النهاية من الوجوه وأثبتها من وجه، فجعل المتناهى غير المتناهي، إذ النهاية حد، والحد قصر عما هو أعظم منه، وذلك تدبير غيره فيه، وهو دليل حدث جانب منه، وذلك جزء، وبعيد كون كلية الأجزاء المتناهية غير متناهية، لأن ذلك المعنى يتمكن في كل جزء منها يتصل، على أن كل واحد منهما في الوجوه التي لا تتناهى إما أن يكون الآخر فيها فيبطل قوله: امتزجا من جانب، بل كانا غير متناه.
A question concerning the description of the sayings of the Dualists: first, the sayings of the Manichaeans and the exposition of their corruption. The Shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: The Manichaeans claimed that things are as they are from the mixture of light and darkness, and they were distinct: light in the high, infinite in four directions: north, south, east, and west; and darkness in the low similarly, and it has from the direction of meeting a finitude. Then darkness crouched upon light, and they mixed, so the world came from their mixture according to the amount of mixture. And each of them has five kinds: redness, whiteness, yellowness, blackness, and greenness. So everything that comes from this kind from the substance of light is good, and what is from the substance of darkness is evil. Likewise, each of them has five senses: hearing, sight, taste, the sense of smell, and touch. So what it perceives of the substance of light through them is good, and what it perceives of the substance of darkness is evil. And light has a spirit, and darkness has a spirit, and the spirit of darkness is called 'Hammāma', and it is a snake. So the world overcame to imprison light in it, and light is not sensitive, and what is from it is by nature and is all good, and the snake (Hammāma) is sensitive, and each of them will return to its own place. Then he found the things: their highest are purest, and their lowest are murkiest, and from their nature are lightness and heaviness, and their affair is based on repulsion, since the light ascends upward and the heavy descends downward. So time passes, while they are thus being purified from the direction of finitude just as they mixed. The Shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: And whoever contemplates the saying finds it all contradictory, without needing to exert oneself in providing evidence for nullifying the saying beyond its interpretation. The first thing in it is that it showed you finitude from some aspects and affirmed it from one aspect, so it made the finite non-finite. For finitude is a limit, and a limit is a restriction from what is greater than it, and that is a management of another in it, and it indicates the occurrence of a part of it, and that is a part. And it is far that the totality of finite parts be non-finite, because that meaning is possible in each part of it that is connected. Moreover, each of the two, in the aspects that are infinite, either the other is in them, which nullifies his saying that they mixed from one side; rather, they were non-finite.
Source pages p. 756

Commentary
This passage is an exposition and refutation of Manichaean dualism. First, Maturidi presents their doctrine: the universe results from the mixing of light (infinite, above) and darkness (finite, below). Darkness invaded light, and the mixture produced the world. Both light and darkness have five genera (colors) and five senses. Light is good, darkness is evil. Light has a spirit; darkness has a spirit called 'Hammāma' (a serpent) that seeks to imprison light. Eventually, each element will separate and return to its own realm. Then Maturidi launches his refutation: the entire doctrine is self-contradictory without needing external evidence. The first contradiction is that the Manichaeans simultaneously affirm finitude and infinity for the same entities. They claim light is infinite in four directions but darkness has finitude at the point of meeting. But if both are infinite, they cannot mix; if one is finite, it implies a limitation imposed by another, indicating createdness. Furthermore, if the parts are finite, the whole cannot be infinite. This reasoning shows the incoherence of the dualistic cosmogony.

منانية
نور
ظلمة
امتزاج
متناه
غير متناه
جنس
حاسة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Manichaeans, what is the role of the serpent spirit (Hammāma)?
A) To create light
B) To imprison light in the world
C) To separate light and darkness
D) To destroy darkness

Key Takeaway
Manichaeans claim the world is a mixture of two eternal principles, light (good) and darkness (evil), which will eventually separate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself blaming 'evil forces' or circumstances for your faults, rather than taking responsibility? The Manichaeans attributed evil to a separate substance. Where in your life are you avoiding personal accountability before Allah by externalizing fault?
?
The Manichaeans believed light (good) was trapped in darkness (evil). In what areas of your life do you feel your good intentions are imprisoned by your habits? How does the Islamic concept of repentance (tawba) offer a way to separate your deeds actively, rather than waiting for a cosmic separation?
?
This passage describes a return of each element to its origin. What kind of separation do you need to make today between your actions that belong to light (obedience) and those that belong to darkness (disobedience)? What is one concrete step you can take right now to disentangle yourself from a mixed state?
